### [322] [FSDBN: Foreground-Aware EEG--Visual Alignment via Dynamic Brain Networks](https://arxiv.org/abs/2607.18344)
*Yiheng Liu,Chuhang Zheng,Peiliang Gong,Jingtao Liu,Daoqiang Zhang,Qi Zhu*

Main category: eess.IV

TL;DR: FSDBN is a unified EEG-visual decoding framework that addresses foreground-background perceptual asymmetry and dynamic brain connectivity, achieving 69.0% top-1 and 92.2% top-5 accuracy on zero-shot brain-to-image retrieval.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing EEG-based visual decoding methods overlook perceptual asymmetry between foreground and background in complex scenes, leading to background interference and semantic misalignment. EEG signals also have rapid temporal dynamics and nonstationary spatial patterns that make it hard to capture time-varying brain connectivity linked to focal visual attention.

Method: FSDBN introduces (1) Semantic-Consistent Saliency Alignment to separate relevant foreground from background noise using joint saliency and semantic constraints; (2) Semantic-Prior Dynamic Gating Foreground Fusion to adaptively regulate foreground/background feature contributions; and (3) adaptive spatiotemporal brain networks that model EEG signals with dynamically reorganizing functional connectivity to capture neural responses to salient foregrounds.

Result: On zero-shot brain-to-image retrieval, FSDBN achieves 69.0% top-1 accuracy and 92.2% top-5 accuracy, outperforming previous state-of-the-art methods.

Conclusion: FSDBN effectively addresses foreground-background asymmetry and dynamic EEG connectivity for robust EEG-visual decoding, with code publicly available.

Abstract: EEG-based visual decoding provides a non-invasive pathway for interpreting visual semantics. However, existing methods often overlook the perceptual asymmetry between foreground and background in complex scenes, leading to background interference and semantic misalignment. EEG signals also exhibit rapid temporal dynamics and nonstationary spatial patterns, making it difficult to capture the time-varying brain connectivity associated with focal visual attention. To address these limitations, we propose FSDBN, a unified framework for robust EEG-visual decoding. FSDBN introduces Semantic-Consistent Saliency Alignment to separate semantically relevant foreground regions from background noise under joint saliency and semantic constraints. It further employs Semantic-Prior Dynamic Gating Foreground Fusion to adaptively regulate the contributions of foreground and background features. In parallel, EEG signals are modeled as adaptive spatiotemporal brain networks whose functional connectivity dynamically reorganizes to capture neural responses to salient foregrounds. Experiments on zero-shot brain-to-image retrieval demonstrate that FSDBN achieves 69.0 percent top-1 accuracy and 92.2 percent top-5 accuracy, outperforming previous state-of-the-art methods. Code is available at https://github.com/LiuYiheng1/FSDBN-EEG.

</details>


### [323] [Thinking Fast, Thinking Slow: Adaptive Multimodal Transformer-based Sensor Fusion for Depth Estimation on Ultra-low-power MCUs](https://arxiv.org/abs/2607.18897)
*Luca Crupi,Lorenzo Lamberti,Giovanni Badaracco,Daniele Allegri,Alessandro Giusti,Daniele Palossi*

Main category: eess.IV

TL;DR: This paper presents an adaptive AI methodology for multimodal sensor fusion (camera, ultrasound, ToF) using a lightweight recurrent Transformer (688k parameters) on an ultra-low-power GAP9 platform, achieving 90% energy savings (2.44 mJ/frame) with only 4.8% δ1 accuracy loss on depth estimation, and outperforming a state-of-the-art model by 31.8% δ1 accuracy under the same power budget (~400 mW).


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To enable reliable multimodal sensor fusion on ultra-low-power (<100 mW) embedded platforms, the paper aims to balance energy consumption and prediction accuracy when adding multiple sensors (camera, ultrasound, ToF) to constrained systems.

Method: A lightweight recurrent Transformer (688k parameters) with token propagation for temporal consistency and a confidence-based gating mechanism that dynamically decides sensor usage per iteration—starting with low-power sensors and incrementally adding more power-demanding ones as needed—deployed on a custom PCB with GAP9 SoC.

Result: On NYUv2: 90% energy saving (2.44 mJ/frame) with only 4.8% δ1 accuracy loss vs. full sensor pipeline; 5.6% lower δ1 than MobileDepth with 9x fewer parameters; 31.8% higher δ1 than a state-of-the-art model on GAP9 under ~400 mW power budget.

Conclusion: The adaptive sensor fusion approach effectively trades minimal accuracy loss for dramatic energy savings, making it highly suitable for ultra-low-power embedded systems, and demonstrates superior accuracy-efficiency trade-offs compared to existing methods.

Abstract: Artificial intelligence (AI)-based multimodal sensor fusion is a relevant topic gaining ever more traction across ultra-low-power (ULP) embedded and cyber-physical systems, as it improves reliability, accuracy, and robustness under real-world constraints. However, adding more and more sensors to ultra-constrained sub-100 mW platforms requires balancing energy consumption against prediction accuracy. To achieve this ambitious goal, we present a novel adaptive AI methodology that combines multimodal sensor fusion (camera, ultrasound, and Time-of-Flight sensors) with a lightweight recurrent Transformer-based architecture (688 k parameters). We address the depth map estimation task with a mechanism that combines token propagation across iterations with incremental sensor utilization. At each iteration, a confidence-based gating mechanism dynamically decides whether to continue the computation by adding progressively richer but more power-demanding sensors as input. Token propagation ensures temporal consistency by forwarding context features across time. To deploy our algorithm and test a first real-world prototype, we design a novel printed circuit board featuring all three sensors, coupled with an ULP GWT GAP9 multicore System-on-Chip. When comparing our adaptive system against the same pipeline using all sensors and iterations on the NYUv2 dataset, we lose only 4.8% of the δ1 accuracy in exchange for 90% energy saving (2.44 mJ/frame). Finally, our adaptive method marks only 5.6% lower δ1 accuracy than MobileDepth despite using 9x fewer parameters. Compared with a state-of-the-art model also running on GAP9, our method improves δ1 accuracy by 31.8% thanks to our adaptive sensor fusion while operating within the same average power budget (~400 mW).

</details>


### [324] [Wavefront Parallelization for Efficient Learned Image Compression](https://arxiv.org/abs/2607.19082)
*Shimon Murai,Fangzheng Lin,Kasidis Arunruangsirilert,Jiro Katto*

Main category: eess.IV

TL;DR: A training-free wavefront acceleration method for autoregressive image compression models that achieves 13× speedup while preserving rate-distortion performance.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Autoregressive context models in learned image compression suffer from slow serial inference, and existing acceleration methods (e.g., checkerboard) require architectural changes and retraining, making them inapplicable to pre-trained models.

Method: Proposes a training-free inference-time acceleration algorithm inspired by wavefront parallelism in video coding standards. Reorganizes inference into an optimal "staggered" wavefront order that minimizes sequential steps while maintaining exact autoregressive dependencies.

Result: Accelerates pre-trained autoregressive models (e.g., Cheng et al.) by more than 13× while preserving original rate-distortion performance; faster decoding is also possible by trading off precise context dependencies.

Conclusion: Wavefront parallelism is an effective, training-free approach to accelerate pre-trained autoregressive image compression models without compromising rate-distortion performance.

Abstract: Autoregressive context models are foundational for learned image compression,but they suffer from slow serial inference. Existing acceleration methods such as checkerboard context require architectural changes and retraining, thus are inapplicable to pre-trained models. We propose a completely training-free inference-time acceleration algorithm inspired by wavefront parallelism in video coding standards. Our method reorganizes inference into an optimal ``staggered'' wavefront order, minimizing sequential steps while maintaining exact autoregressive dependencies. Experimental results show our approach accelerates pre-trained autoregressive models (e.g., Cheng et al.) by more than $13\times$ while preserving the original rate-distortion performance. We also demonstrate that faster decoding is possible by trading off precise context dependencies. Source code will be available at https://github.com/tokkiwa/compressai-wavefront.

</details>


### [325] [Fast reconstruction of tensor tomographic X-ray scattering data for real-time applications](https://arxiv.org/abs/2607.19124)
*André M. Antunes,Daniël M. Pelt,K. Joost Batenburg*

Main category: eess.IV

TL;DR: A direct reconstruction method for X-ray scattering tensor tomography that replaces slow iterative reconstruction with algebraic filters and a single back-projection step, achieving over 10x speedup and enabling real-time imaging.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing X-ray scattering tensor tomography relies on slow iterative reconstruction, limiting real-time use and high-throughput analysis. The authors aim to overcome this computational bottleneck.

Method: The approach extends direct reconstruction for parallel-beam geometries by computing algebraic filters that approximate multiple iterative updates in a single filtering and back-projection step. It explicitly separates the tomographic projector from a view-dependent mixing operator, generalizing across tensor representations and X-ray scattering measurement modes.

Result: The method approximates iterative reconstructions while reducing computation time by over an order of magnitude. A 53×53×53×28 tensor volume is reconstructed in 1 second on commercially-available hardware.

Conclusion: The speed and stability of this approach enable high-throughput analysis and real-time scattering-based imaging.

Abstract: X-ray scattering tensor tomography reveals nanoscale structural orientation in 3D, but its reliance on slow iterative reconstruction limits real-time use. We introduce an extension of a direct reconstruction approach for parallel-beam geometries that computes algebraic filters approximating multiple iterative updates with a single filtering and back-projection step. By explicitly separating the tomographic projector from a view-dependent mixing operator, the method generalizes across tensor representations and modes of (small-angle) X-ray scattering measurement. Simulated and experimental results show that the approach approximates iterative reconstructions while reducing computation time by over an order of magnitude, realizing a reconstruction of a 53x53x53x28 tensor volume in 1 second on commercially-available hardware. The resulting speed and stability enable high-throughput analysis and open the door to real-time scattering-based imaging.

</details>


### [326] [MIRAGE: Multi-scale Lesion-Informed Representation with Auxiliary Guidance for MRI Contrast Enhancement](https://arxiv.org/abs/2607.19137)
*Andrea Borghesi,Xin Wang,Jonas Teuwen,George Yiasemis*

Main category: eess.IV

TL;DR: MIRAGE introduces a residual U-Net with lesion-aware supervision (asymmetric penalty, multi-scale segmentation, frozen nnU-Net guidance) for synthesizing post-contrast breast MRI from pre-contrast scans, outperforming generative baselines on lesion localization while revealing a fidelity-utility trade-off.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Inferring contrast enhancement from a single pre-contrast breast MRI slice is underdetermined; optimizing only pixel fidelity can suppress lesion enhancement, while adversarial/stochastic objectives may lack patient-specific lesion fidelity.

Method: A residual 2D U-Net (MIRAGE) trained with global reconstruction, perceptual losses, and three lesion-aware supervision signals: asymmetric penalty for missed tumor enhancement, multi-scale auxiliary tumor segmentation, and guidance from a frozen post-contrast tumor segmentation nnU-Net.

Result: MIRAGE ranks first on six of eight metrics on 301 multi-centre cases, markedly improving downstream lesion localization over pix2pix, conditional diffusion, and latent bridge-matching baselines. Generative baselines retain advantages in LPIPS/contrast classification, showing a fidelity-utility trade-off.

Conclusion: Task-aware synthesis can be conditionally optimal, but its superiority depends on the downstream models and metrics used to define utility; the three lesion-aware losses are partly redundant for localization but exert distinct effects on appearance, radiomics, and boundary accuracy.

Abstract: Inferring contrast enhancement from one pre-contrast breast MRI slice is underdetermined: post-contrast appearance contains physiological information that is not uniquely encoded in baseline anatomy. Optimizing only paired pixel fidelity can suppress uncertain lesion enhancement, whereas adversarial or stochastic generative objectives can favor realistic post-contrast appearance without guaranteeing patient-specific lesion fidelity. We introduce MIRAGE, a residual 2D U-Net that combines global reconstruction and perceptual losses with three forms of lesion-aware supervision available only during training: an asymmetric penalty for missed tumor enhancement, multi-scale auxiliary tumor segmentation, and guidance through a frozen post-contrast tumor segmentation nnU-Net. We evaluate the method on 301 cases from the multi-centre MAMA-SYNTH data using eight complementary image-, region-, radiomics-, and segmentation-based metrics. MIRAGE ranks first on six metrics and markedly improves downstream lesion localization over tuned pix2pix, conditional diffusion, and latent bridge-matching baselines. The generative alternatives retain advantages in LPIPS or contrast classification, revealing a clear fidelity-utility trade-off. Leave-one-in and leave-one-out ablations show that the losses are partly redundant for lesion localization but exert distinct effects on appearance, radiomics, and boundary accuracy. These results support task-aware synthesis while also showing that its apparent optimality is conditional on the downstream models and metrics used to define utility.

</details>
